The Three-Fold Classification of Categorical Propositions
Classification of categorical propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any categorical proposition as external, mental, or real based on the mode of existence of its subject.

Core Idea
A categorical proposition's type depends on whether its subject is external, mental, or both.

In this passage, the author introduces a classification of categorical propositions based on the ontological status of the subject. Understanding these categories is crucial for analyzing how propositions relate to reality and for avoiding confusion in logical and theological discussions. We will walk through the three primary types and their subtypes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the proposition
Look at the term about which something is affirmed or denied. This is the subject (al-mawdu').
Ensure you have the correct subject; it may be implicit or explicit.
2
Determine the mode of existence of the subject
Is the subject considered as an actual external object (kharijiyya), a mental concept (dhihniyya), or both (haqiqiyya mutlaqa)?
'Actual' includes both existing and hypothetical (muqaddar).
3
Classify the proposition accordingly
If the subject is external (actual or assumed), the proposition is external (kharijiyya). If mental, it is mental (dhihniyya). If absolute (both), it is real absolutely (haqiqiyya mutlaqa).
Al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq confirms this tripartite classification.
4
Apply to given examples
Test the classification on examples: natural propositions are external; propositions of this 'art' (logic) are mental; geometrical propositions are real absolute.
This helps solidify the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تبصرة في تحقيق المحصورات الذَّهْنِيَّةُ ، أَوْ مُقَدَّرٍ)، أي غير معتبر التحقق بخصوصه، سواء كان محققا أو مفروضا ، (وَهِيَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ الذَّهْنِيَّةُ ، أَوْ أَمْرِ خَارِجِي مُحَقَّقِ ، وَهِيَ الْخَارِجِيَّةُ ، أَوْ مُقَدَّرٍ) بذلك المعنى، (وَهِيَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ الْخَارِجِيَّةُ، أَوْ مُطْلَقًا)، سواء كان ذهنيا محققا أو مقدرا، أو خارجيا كذلك، (وَهِيَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ عَلَى الْإِطْلَاقِ، كَالْقَضَايَا الْهَنْدَسِيَّةِ وَالْحِسَابِيَّةِ). قال السيد المحقق قدس سره الشريف: القضية إن حكم فيها بثبوت المحمول للموضوع الخارجي محققا أو مقدرا فخارجية، كالقضايا الطبعية، والذهني المحقق أو المقدر فذهنية، كقضايا هذا الفن، أو مطلقا فحقيقية، كالقضايا الهندسية، ولا أجد لتغير الاصطلاح إلى ما ذكره المصنف، وتكثير مفهومات القضايا فائدة متعدة بها، قال صاحب الأفق المبين: الحملية إن حكم فيها على البت فبتية، وإن حكم فيها على تقدير ثبوت العنوان فغير بتية، وهي مساوقة للشرطية.
A note on the verification of quantified propositions: (the mental, or the assumed), i.e., not considering realization specifically, whether actual or hypothetical, (and it is the mental real, or an external actual thing, and it is the external, or the assumed) in that sense, (and it is the external real, or absolute), whether mental actual or assumed, or external likewise, (and it is the real absolutely, like geometrical and arithmetic propositions). Al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq (may his secret be sanctified) said: A proposition, if judgment is made in it of the subject's possession of the predicate as actual or assumed, it is external, like natural propositions; if mental actual or assumed, it is mental, like propositions of this art; if absolute, it is real, like geometrical propositions. And I do not find any benefit in changing the terminology to what the author mentioned and multiplying the concepts of propositions. The author of al-Ufuq al-Mubin said: The categorical proposition, if judgment in it is categorical, it is categorical; if judgment in it is upon the condition of the existence of the term, it is non-categorical, and it is equivalent to the conditional.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage defines and expands the classification of categorical propositions (qadaya hamliyya) based on the mode of existence of the subject. The author begins by detailing types: mental (dhihniyya) referring to what exists in the mind either actually or hypothetically, external (kharijiyya) referring to actual external existence, and absolute (mutlaqa) which covers both. These correspond to 'mental real', 'external real', and 'real absolutely'. Examples include geometrical propositions being absolute reals. Al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq then clarifies: if judgment is about an external subject (actual or assumed), it is external; if about a mental subject, it is mental; if absolute, it is real. He criticizes the author's multiplication of concepts as useless. Finally, al-Ufuq al-Mubin introduces another distinction: categorical propositions are either decisive (batiiyya) if judged unconditionally, or conditional (ghayr batiiyya) if judged on condition of the existence of the term, equating the latter with conditional propositions.

Key Terms
القضية الحقيقية
القضية الخارجية
القضية الذهنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Categorical propositions are classified as external, mental, or real based on the mode of existence of their subject, and this classification is essential for logical analysis in Islamic sciences.

The Distinction Between Decisive and Conditional Propositions
Al-Ufuq's distinction between decisive and conditional propositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a decisive (batiiyya) and a conditional (ghayr batiiyya) categorical proposition and convert the latter into a conditional proposition.

Core Idea
A categorical proposition can be either unconditional in judgment or conditional on the existence of its subject term.

Al-Ufuq al-Mubin introduces a further division of categorical propositions: some are decisive (batiiyya), where the judgment holds without qualification; others are non-decisive (ghayr batiiyya), where the judgment is contingent upon the existence of the subject. This distinction is equivalent to that between absolute and conditional propositions, and it helps avoid ambiguity in logical and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Examine the judgment in the proposition
Determine whether the predicate is affirmed or denied of the subject in an unconditional manner or if it depends on some condition.
The condition here is the existence of the subject (thubut al-'unwan).
2
Check if the judgment depends on the subject's existence
If the proposition is only true when the subject exists (i.e., the judgment is conditioned on the actuality of the subject), it is non-decisive (ghayr batiiyya).
Example: 'The Phoenix is a bird' is false if the subject does not exist, but the proposition might be intended conditionally.
3
Identify the type accordingly
If the judgment holds without any condition on the subject's existence, it is decisive (batiiyya). Otherwise, it is non-decisive and equivalent to a conditional proposition.
Al-Ufuq equates non-decisive categoricals with conditional propositions (shartiyya).
4
Test with an example from the text
Consider 'Every human is an animal' – if taken unconditionally, it is decisive. But if taken conditionally (e.g., 'If a human exists, then it is an animal'), it is non-decisive.
The same wording can have different logical forms depending on intended meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تبصرة في تحقيق المحصورات الذَّهْنِيَّةُ ، أَوْ مُقَدَّرٍ)، أي غير معتبر التحقق بخصوصه، سواء كان محققا أو مفروضا ، (وَهِيَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ الذَّهْنِيَّةُ ، أَوْ أَمْرِ خَارِجِي مُحَقَّقِ ، وَهِيَ الْخَارِجِيَّةُ ، أَوْ مُقَدَّرٍ) بذلك المعنى، (وَهِيَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ الْخَارِجِيَّةُ، أَوْ مُطْلَقًا)، سواء كان ذهنيا محققا أو مقدرا، أو خارجيا كذلك، (وَهِيَ الْحَقِيقِيَّةُ عَلَى الْإِطْلَاقِ، كَالْقَضَايَا الْهَنْدَسِيَّةِ وَالْحِسَابِيَّةِ). قال السيد المحقق قدس سره الشريف: القضية إن حكم فيها بثبوت المحمول للموضوع الخارجي محققا أو مقدرا فخارجية، كالقضايا الطبعية، والذهني المحقق أو المقدر فذهنية، كقضايا هذا الفن، أو مطلقا فحقيقية، كالقضايا الهندسية، ولا أجد لتغير الاصطلاح إلى ما ذكره المصنف، وتكثير مفهومات القضايا فائدة متعدة بها، قال صاحب الأفق المبين: الحملية إن حكم فيها على البت فبتية، وإن حكم فيها على تقدير ثبوت العنوان فغير بتية، وهي مساوقة للشرطية.
